17.   SALARY OF THE STAFF
In order to engage competent candidates with qualification and experience
required to perform the functions specified in Section 16 above, the Board shall
fix the salary of the staff within the range given below:
a)    Executive Director              Rs. 35,000/-       to    45,000/-
b)    Deputy Executive Director       Rs, 30,000/-       to    40,000/-
c)    Chiefs of the Unit              Rs. 25,000/-       to    35,000/-
d)    Professional Staff              Rs. 20,000/-       to    30,000/-
e)    Support Staffs
-     Senior Secretary         Rs. 10,000/-        to    12,000/-
-     Assistant MIS Officer   Rs. 10,000/-         to    12,000/-
-     Accountant               Rs. 10,000/-        to    12,000/-
-     Secretary                Rs.  6,000/-        to     8,000/-
-     Receptionist             Rs.  6,000/-        to     8,000/-
-     Driver                   Rs.  3,000/-        to     5,000/-
-     Messenger                Rs.  3,000/-        to     4,000/-
-     Watchman                 Rs.  3,000/-        to     4,000/-
18.   DASAIN ALLOWANCE
Every staff shall get Dasain Allowance annually equivalent to one month's salary.
19.   VEHICLE FACILITY
Office vehicles shall be used strictly for official purposes and they shall not
be used for pick ups and drop offs of the staff.
20.   LEAVE
1.    National Holidays
The staffs shall be entitled to twelve days of national holidays as
specified in schedule C.
2.    Annual Leavo
The staff shall get 2.2 calendar days per month as annual leave with full
pay.
3.    Sick Leave
The staffs shall get 6 calendar days per year as sick leave with full pay.
4.    Maternity Leave
Female staff shall be entitled to a total of 60 days maternity leave with
full pay.
5.    Leave Without Pay
Any other leave not covered by the above clauses shall be leave without
pay and shall not be taken unless approved by the Chairperson of the Board
in case of the Executive Director and by the Executive Director in case of
any other staff.  However, such leave without pay shall not exceed 10
percent of total working days in a year.
6.    Accumulation of Leave
Paid leave shall not be accumulated and shall lapse at the end of every
year.
a)    Provided unused annual leave shall be accumulated maximum upto
15 days during the terms of his office and shall be paid at the end
of his service.



- 89 -
Annex 6
Page 9 of II
b)    Provided that all leave except sick leave shall not be taken
unless approved by the Chairperson of the Board in case of the
Executive Director and by the Executive Director in case of any
other staff.
21.   MEDICAL FACILITIES
In the event of sickness the staff shall be entitled to 70% of the total medical
expenses incurred.  However, for the entire service period of the staff such
facility shall not exceed one month's equivalent salary of the staff.
22.   DAILY ALLOWANCE
The daily allowance for the field visit outside the Kathmandu valley shall be Rs.
350/- for all staff.
23.   TRAVELLING ALLOWANCE
The travel allowance shall be on the basis of actual cost incurred. The mode of
transport allowed for the staff of the Board and Support Agency staff shall be
determined by the Executive Director on the basis of policy guidelines issued by
the Board. However it shall not be allowed to any staff travelling by the office
vehicle.
24.   WORKING HOURS
The normal working hour for the staff shall be from 9:00 AM to 5:00 PM six days
a week with half an hour lunch break in the afternoon.   The executive and
professional staff shall not be entitled to overtime payment and the Support
staff shall get overtime payment at the rate of 1.5 times the salary converted
to the hourly rate.
25.   OFFICIAL SECRECY
No staff shall disclose the official secrets or pass on secret documents without
the permission of the Board or the Executive Director.
26.   EXCLUSIVE EMPLOYMENT
No staff shall engage in any other job during the time of his recruitment by the
Board.
27.   DISCIPLINARY ACTION
1.    Disciplinary Action against the Executive Director
The Board, while taking disciplinary action against the Executive Director
under Section 8 (5) of the Order, shall follow the procedure as follows:
-     ask for written explanation to clarify the charge against him within
15 days;
-     issue  a  letter  of  warning  or dismissal  from  service  if  the
explanation submitted is not satisfactory.
Every dismissal order shall explain the reasons for action taken.
2.    Disciplinary Action against the Executive Staff
The Board shall have the power to take disciplinary action against the
Executive and Professional Staff on the recommendation of the Executive
Director for incapacity, corruption or unsatisfactory performance of his
duty. The procedure for such disciplinary action shall be as follows:



- 90 -
Annex 6
Page 10 of 11
-     ask for written explanation to clarify the charge against him within
15 days;
-     issue  a  letter  of  warning  or dismissal  from  service  if  the
explanation submitted is not satisfactory.
Every dismissal order shall explain the reasons for action taken.
3.    Disciplinary Action against the Support Staffs
The Executive Director shall have the power to take disciplinary action
against the Support Staff for incapacity, corruption or unsatisfactory
performance of his duty. The procedure for such disciplinary action shall
be as follows:
-     ask for written explanation to clarify the charge against him within
15 days;
-     issue  a  letter  of  warning  or dismissal  from  service  if  the
explanation submitted is not satisfactory.
Every dismissal order shall explain the reasons for action taken.
FINANCIAL ADMINISTRATION
28.   ACCOUNTING
a)    The books of account of the Board shall be kept in a commercial
(double entry) accrual accounting system.
b)    The Board shall have a separate account for day to day operations of
the office and Project account for financing projects.
c)    The Project account will record the funds advanced to the Support
Organizations and User Groups from time to time and expenditures incurred
by them on authorized project activities.
d)    The Fund will maintain a petty cash account to meet its minor
expenses. A specific amount as authorized by the Board shall be kept in
petty cash account.
e)    The account of the Board shall be operated by the joint signature of
the Executive Director and the Chief of the Administration Unit.
29.   BUDGET PREPARATION
(1)   Chief of the Administration Unit shall prepare the budget for each
fiscal year at least 60 days before the commencement of the fiscal year
which shall be reviewed by the Executive Director before presentation to
the Board for approval.
(2)   In case the amount allocated for any line item in the budget is
inadequate the Executive Director shall have the authority to transfer up
to 10 percent of the amount of one budget heading to another budget
heading without affecting the annual program of the Board. Any transfer
greater than 10 percent shall be done with the approval of the Board.
30.   PROCUREMENT
(1)   The procurement of goods and services including consultant for the
*Board shall be made by the Chief of Administration Unit in consultation
with the various functional units of the Board and Approval by Executive
Director. IDA procurement guidelines will be followed for the procurement
of such goods and services.



- 91 -
Annex 6
Pa2e II ofr I
(2)   Procurement  of  services  of  Support  Organizations  as  service
providers shall be made on the basis of eligibility criteria provided in
the Rules through direct contracting procedures. Projects (schemes) will
be selected on demand driven basis, using its eligibility criteria.
(3)   Procurement of goods and services by Support Organizations and
contracted parties shall be done independently but the Board will set up
basic norms and standards to check price, quality, quantity and other
necessary requisites. The Chief of the Administration Unit will ensure
efficiency and economy by comparing a Support Organizations' cost proposal
with a schedule of standard unit costs and prices it would develop and
update from time to time with the approval of the Technical Appraisal
Committee.
MISCELLANEOUS
31.   DELEGATION OF AUTHORITY
a)    Delegation of authority by the Board under Section 13(1) of the
Order shall be made through a written letter of authorization specifying
the objective, duration and the specific activity authorized to be taken.
Provided that the Board may withdraw the delegated authority any
time through written notice.
b)    Delegation of authority by the Executive Director under Section 13
(2) of the order shall be made through a written letter of authorization
specifying the objectives, duration and the activity authorized to be
taken.
Provided that the Executive Director may withdraw the delegated
authority any time through written notice.
32.   ALLOWANCE TO THE BOARD MEMBERS
Each Member attending the Board meeting shall be entitled for meeting allowance
of NRs. 800/- per meeting.   The Chairperson shall be entitled for a meeting
allowance of NRs. 1000/- for each meeting chaired.
33.   REPORTING
The Executive Director shall make quarterly reporting to the Board. The report
shall include the financial statement of the Board and progress made in
implementation of the annual program.

Terms of Reference:
1.     Executive Director (ED)
General:
The Executive Director is the senior position within Fund Board Secretariat. The ED will be
responsible to operationalize, manage, and implement the policies and decisions of the Fund-Board
so as to fulfill its mandate. The ED will work closely with local govemment, NGOs and the private
sector Support Organizations. The ED will have a particular focus on ensuring that all Fund Board
operations and functions are performing, and retains overall responsibility for personnel and their
performance. The ED provided active support to the Board, providing the board with information
needed and recommendations for appropriate action. The ED is responsible for ensuring the
qualitative output of the Fund-Board's work in terms of providing services which ensure greater equity
and sustainability of rural water supply and sanitation services. The ED also ensures that Fund-Board
operations remain adaptive and responsive to lessons learned and demands from the field.
Specific:
1.     Execute the policies, annual programs and budgets as approved by the Board.
2.    Manage the overall program of the Fund Board, including supervision of the Units of the,
Secretariat and their related operating systems and provide technical inputs as needed.
3.    Oversee personnel management, including the recruitment of the executive staff with Board
approval.
4.     Liaise with partner agencies (SOs, and SAs) in all matters pertaining to solicitation,
contracting and completion of schemes and provision of related services to communities.
5.     Oversee the analysis of program outputs and related processes and provide direction in the
preparation of appropriate mechanisms, systems, tools and guidelines.
6.     Oversee the progress of the portfolio of schemes of the Fund-Board. Chair the Technical
Appraisal Committee (TAC) meetings and review submissions to the Board.
7.     Supervise the Administrative staff in maintenance of the administrative, personnel and
financial records.
8.     Liaise with all agencies working in the sector, and help evolve appropriate policies and
support for further development and improvements of RWSS In Nepal.



Annex 6
- 94-                             Schedule B
Page 2 of 16
Terms of Reference:
2.     Deputy Executive Director (DED)
General:
The Deputy Executive Director is primarily responsible for day to-day operations of the Fund
Board. The DED is responsible for coordination of the various units of the fund on a functional basis,
and to ensure that operational systems are working. The DED calls and coordinates regular meetings
of secretariat staff, including TAC meetings for which the DED ensures preparation of appropriate
documentation. The DED has primary responsibility for Management Information Systems of the
Fund Board and ensures the flow of information is maintained to all appropriate units. The DED is
active in managing the recruitment of SAs to provide services for the project, and in checking on all
key steps in the scheme review process. The DED acts for the Executive Director in his/her absence.
Specific:
1.     Ensure that all units are working together to maintain the progress of their respective
functions.
2.     Supervises the preparation of the budgets to be submitted to the Fund Board
3.     Oversee the MIS systems and make sure that all key program information is recorded,
processed and disseminated on a timely basis.
4.     Ensure timely processing of procurement of SO/SA services and time payments.
5.     Liaise with SOs and communities to help overcome constraints they may face in achieving
project objectives.
6.     Organize the work of the Technical Appraisal Committee and ensure preparations for TAC
meetings. Review progress of each portfolio manager on a regular basis. Schedule and
review documentation to be presented at TAC meetings. Ensure that recommendations from
TAC meetings are prepared for Board presentation.
7.    Initiate and undertake the SO financial audits. Engage a competent SA for this work and
oversee the auditing process.
8.     Prepare overall portfolio progress reports. Assist the ED in preparation of reports to the
management board.
9.     The DED undertakes the liaison work with the Local Government in coordination with the
Portfolio Managers. The DED will make sure, that the District Development Committees are
contacted and informed in the necessary points of the project cycle.
10.    Prepare the necessary reporting, e.g. the Quarterly Reports, to the Board.
11.    Undertake the duties of the ED in her/his absence.

The Operations/M & E Unit Chief has the overall responsibility of the program issues, overseeing the

Recommend action to be taken.

14.   Act in the capacity of the DED in his/her absence

4      Human Resource Development/Program Development Unit Chief
General:
The HRD/Program Development Unit Chief provides guidelines for the software components of the
project. S/he Is responsible for making arrangements for training and assistance to
SOs/communities, based on assessments of capacity building needs. This includes identification,
solicitation, and recruitment of Service Agencies and consultants. S/he provides analysis of software
as part of the TAC during scheme processing. S/he also assesses program development issues
related to software emerging from field experience and reports, and recommends measures to
improve the quality software activities and Inputs. S/he also oversees design and production of
training and communications support Initiatives and materials.
1.     Prepare the necessary manpower assessments and training plans for the Fund.
2.     Prepare and present the SO staff selection criteria for different job categories (for the staff to
be funded by the Fund Board).
3.     Conduct and coordinate the screening process for the staff suggested by the SOs.
4.     Assist the Portfolio managers in the contract negotiations, especially in the manpower and
staffing questions.
5.    Identification and preparation, for the use of SO's necessary materials, especially to be used
in participatory decision making in the village.
6.     Coordinate all the training activities organized by the Fund Board.
7.     As a special point of emphasis, plan and implement a training course in community
(participatory) monitoring.
8.     Engage qualified Service Agencies for implementing the training activities.
9.     Assess the impact of the training activities by visiting the trained staff in the field and
monitoring their performance.
10.    Assist the Operations/M & E Unit Chief to prepare the Terms of Reference and engage
qualified Service Agencies to undertake the monitoring of the software activities.
11.   Assess the quality of the Service Agencies' work and give recommendations to the
Operations/Montoring and Evaluation Unit Chief, especially in relation to the software and
training activitles.

Terms of Reference:
5.     Technical Unit Chief
General:
The Chief of the Technical Unit is responsible for the oversight of the technical aspects of the
RWSSP. A key responsibility is to assess the technical capability of SOs to determine their eligibility
to participate in RWSSP and to develop strategies for strengthening their capability. This will Include
recruitment and training of service agencies for strengthening technical staff. Also fundamental to the
position is managing the technical appraisal of scheme proposals, and ensuring that project designs
are prepared in a community-based approach in which key decisions are taken by users. Reviews of
project submissions Include application of field-tested technical guidelines, standards and
specifications for hardware. The Unit head prepares unit prices and norms and applies them to
proposed cost estimates. He/she participates in TAC meetings and manages all record keeping with
reference to the technical aspects of the RWSSP.
Specific:
1.    Identification, field testing and recommendation to the Board of a range of technical
standards to be accepted as the basis of the community water supply design.
2.     Follow-up and updating of the unit costs and prices of the community water supply schemes.
3.    Preparing the price and quality norms to be followed by the SOs in the procurement of
materials.
4.     Appraise the technical proposals and the BOQs against the corresponding site appraisals
and present them for approval/rejection to the TAC.
5.     Assist the Portfolio Managers in the contract negotiations in respect to the hardware
components. This work includes verification of the estimates and (unit) prices included in the
BO, and checking of bills submitted for payment against the accepted price/quality norms.
6.     Assist the Operations/M & E Unit in identifying, writing the Terms of Reference and
engaging qualified Service Agencies for the site appraisals and quality control of the water
supply systems (hardware component).
7.    Assist the HRD/Program Development Unit in assessing the technical capability of SOs and
SAs
8.    Assist the HRD/Program in the selection of SAs in the technical training
9.     Assist Operations/M&E Unit in appraising the performance and quality of the technical work
undertaken by the SAs in monitoring of the field activities
10.    Assist in the community monitoring training, emphasis on the community's quality control of
the procurement and construction quality.
i1.   Assist the HRD/ Prog. Dev. Unit in design and development of training courses and materials
for engineers, Overseers, Technicians, VMWs
12.    Provide advice to SOs on issues related to procurement of hardware materials
13.    Supervise the Engineer of the Technical Unit.

6.     Administrative Unit Chief
General:
Oversees the administration of the Fund-Board Secretariat, including financial management,
procurement and contract management, and personnel. Undertakes detailed management of Support
Organization and Support Agency procurement for the Fund Board. Prepares and tracks budget
information and advises management. Manages contracts for the Development Phase and
ImplementationlPost-Implementation Phase, and ensures thorough documentation of all contract and
procurement processes related to scheme implementation by SOs/communities and technical
services provided by Service Agencies. Take responsibility for overseeing procurement issues
related to SO/SA contracts, and provide logistical support to contractors. Oversees finance
management of the Fund Board, and manages the Administrative and Accounts staff. Provides
financial and management information on the status of all contracts.

2.    Management of the internal procurement of the Fund Board.

and assist in Fund-Board audits.

7.     Ensure proper management of contract payments and ensure that necessary financial
statements have been submitted by the SOs.

9.    Supervise support staff of the Fund Board Secretariat

S.     HSE and WTSS Program Development Officer
HSE related:
General:
Strengthen the HSE component of schemes. Assist SOs/communities with definition of
specific HSE strategies and continuously assist SOs to refine alternative HSE strategies, data
gathering activities, practices, procedures, training methods and educational resources. Monitor the
progress of the HSE aspects of the project. Assist in the recruitment of SAs for HSE. Manage a
portfolio of schemes and participate in the TAC and project review process.
The primary responsibility of this post is the portfolio management and the post holder will work as
HSE specialist when the work load relating to portfolio management allow.
Specifically:
1.     Assist the Portfolio Mangers in assessing the health and education activities proposed by the
SOs. Assess their cost efficiency.
2 .    Assist the Portfolio Mangers in screening the Health Facilitator staff proposed by the SOs.

3 .   Review and identify suitable health and sanitation related training materials and recommend
to SOs to be used in their field based training.
4.     Assist the HRD/Program Development Unit to plan, design and undertake health and
sanitation related training and orientation to the SOs.
5.     Assess the efficiency of the health and sanitation activities by periodic field visits.
6.     Assess the efficiency and verify the reliability and quality of the SAs work in the field of
health education and sanitation.
WTSS related:
General:
The Women Technical Support Services Officer assists in gender issues related to the
policies and operations of the Fund-Board. S/he monitors gender issues within the operations and
schemes of the Fund Board and ensures compliance with criteria for women's involvement are met
by SOs/communities. S/he is responsible for developing the resources and assisting SOs and SAs to
incorporate the women's technical services component of the RWSSP. This especially implies
helping SOs staff and communities access credit linkages and training. S/he recruits SAs for training
and orientation of women about credit and income opportunities, and helps orient SAs who provide
general training to SOs to include training such as gender analysis and planning.
Specific:
1.     Recommends policies and criteria related to gender as part of the Fund-Board's policies and
procedures.
2.     Reviews portfolios of projects in terms of gender. Ensures compliance with requirements for
women's participation and membership within WUCs.

Termns of Reference:
9.     Engineer
General:
The Engineer has primary responsibility for quality control In terms of SO procurement of
materials. S/he also assists in monitoring the submissions of receipts and invoices for materials by
SOs/communities, and checks cost estimates against actual procurement to see if purchases are
within reasonable facsimile of the approved design estimates. The engineer assists in the
documentation of technical aspects of projects, and participates in portfolio management.
Specific:
1 .    Checks on the quality of materials being supplied to SOs/communities. Recruits specialist
help where necessary for this purpose.
2.     monitors,contract compliance in terms of procurement of materials by SOs. Notes major
discrepancies between design estimates and materials actually procured. Assists SOs to
procure materials effectively.
3.     provides assistance in the analysis of project designs.
4.    maintains records on technical aspects of schemes.
5.     assists in orientation of SAs and in the training and provision of technical assistance to SOs.
6.     provides assistance to the PM's in undertaking the site appraisals and quality control of the
hardware in the field.



- 103 -
Annex 6
Schedule B
Pagc I I of 16
Tenns of Reference:
10.   Information Management Officer
General:
The information Management Officer (IMO) assists in the management and handling of data
emerging from the M&E system. S/he is responsible to ensure data Is translated, recorded, compiled
and analyzed. This includes the planning of a system for analysis of data and selection of appropriate
software for data analysis. The data analyst will work with project staff and provide information
needed for project decisions, and be the key person responsible for the MIS on a day-to-day basis.
Specific:
1.     Prepare the field information collected for coding and data entry.
2.     Update the databases as defined by the Operations/Monitoring and Evaluation Unit Chief.
3.    Selection of appropriate software for data analysis and design a system for analyzing and
storing the field data. Undertake he necessary programming work.
4.    Issue necessary summaries of the data base to Portfolio Mangers, Operations/M & Unit, ED
etc.
5.     Produce necessary summary tables for the Fund and the Quarterly Progress Reports.



- 104 -                              Annex 6
Schedule B
Pagc 12 of 16
Tenns of Reference:
II.    Portfolio Manager
General:
The Portfolio Manager (PM) is responsible for ensuring contractual compliance of the Support
Organization (SOs), the Communities and the Fund Board. The PM is the link ensuring that the
communities are provided the services of a quality, by the SOs, to enable them to prepare for,
manage, construct, maintain & operate their own schemes. The PM is responsible to keep, maintain
and provide to the management all relevant information pertaining to an SO and their respective
schemes.
Specific:
A.    Pre-Development Phase
1      Selection of the Support Organizations
-      Assist in the Evaluation of the old and new SOs, and in particular the assessment of
their previous "Track Record".
-      Assist in the Pre-feasibility orientation training to the SOs.
2.     Pre-feasibility and Site/Scheme selection
-      Assist in the evaluation of the Pre-feasibility proposals.
-      Undertake Pre-feasibility site appraisals by visiting the SO sites/scheme site.
3.     Development Phase Contract preparation
-      Advise SOs in the preparation of their "Development Phase Proposals"
-      Negotiate with the SOs concerned, on their financial and activity details of the
proposals.
-      Ensure that all pre-requisites and criteria have been met prior to the finalization of
the "Development Phase Contract" including to ensure that the SO staff proposed
are qualified and competent as per required standards.
-      Prepare all relevant documents and submit the Development Phase Proposal to the
TAC.
-      Supervise the Development Phase Contract preparation.
B.    Development Phase
1      SO Staff Selection and Orientation
-      Assist the Human Resource Development/Program Development Unit (HRD/PDU) in
orientation training and other training's necessary for the SOs.
-      Ensure that the SO is aware of and attends scheduled training's and ensure that the
SO receives the feedback on how its staff performed in the training's.
-      Ensure that the staff engaged are those which were proposed and agreed upon.
2      Contract performance monitoring
-      Monitor contractual performance by the SOs through field visits or coordinated field
visits made by the SA on his/her behalf.
-      Monitor time spent by the SO staff in the field and ensure that they have undertaken
and achieved activities as specified in the proposal till the monitored period.
-      Identify SO and Community weaknesses to be addressed by the SO and make
recommendations with possible solutions in the area of weaknesses.
-      Provide feedback / comments to the SOs of monitoring visits by providing them with
a copy of monitoring report. Ensure that the feedback given to the SO are
immediately acted upon.
-      Ensure that the Contract Completion Report is made by the SO. This Contract
Completion Report should also be endorsed by him / her.
3      Contract payments
-      Ensure that the request for payment are made in time by the SOs and verify that the
payment conditions are met as specified in the contract.
-      Recommend payments and sign the payment recommendation memorandum.

Terms of reference: (Continued) 10. Portfolio Manager
C.    Implementation Phase
1.    Preparation
Check the completeness of the Implementation Phase Proposal, Progress Report
and Financial Statement fumished by the SOs and review It. Incomplete proposals
shall be promptly notified to the SOs.
Check the completeness of the Technical Proposal and forward t to the Technical
Unit upon being satisfied. Incomplete proposals shall be notified to the SO
immediately.
Make field visit and I or identify SAs to appraise the Implementation Proposal in
conjunction with the Third Payment Monitoring visit.
Keep track of the Proposal under review.
Conclude Implementation Proposals and negotiate the Financial Proposal of the SO I
Community.
Ensure that the criteria are met in the Proposals and prepare the Proposal
Assessment Fomms.
- Present the Proposal to the TAC for approval.
Supervise and assist the Administration in the preparation of the Implementation
Phase Contracts.
Ensure that the Implementation Contracts are signed according to the requirements
2.    Contract performance monitoring
-     Monitor contractual performance by the SOs through field visits or coordinated field
visits made by the SA on his/her behalf.
-     Monitor time spent by the SO staff in the field and ensure that they have undertaken
and achieved activities as specified In the Community Action Plan (CAP) till the
monitored period.
-     Identify SO and Community weaknesses to be addressed by the SO and make
recommendations with possible solutions in the area of weaknesses.
-     Provide feedback / comments to the SOs of monitoring visits and construction
monitoring visits by providing them with a copy of monitoring report. Ensure that the
feedback given to the SO are Immediately acted upon.
-     Keep track of the activities being conducted by the SOs during the Contract period
and acting immediately on deviations reflecting to the planned activities.
3     Contract payment
Ensure that the request for payment are made in time by the SOs and verify that the
payment conditions are met as specified in the contract.
Recommend payments and sign the payment recommendation memorandum.
4     Scheme Completion report
Ensure that the Contract Completion Report Is made by the SO. This Contract
Completion Report should also be endorsed by him / her.
Based on the Contract Completion Report of the Development, Implementation and
Post Implementation Phase prepared by the SO, the PM shall prepare a Scheme
Completion Report which he / she submits with his / her recommendation for the
Third payment to the ED.

Terms of Reference:
12.    Information Assistant
The Information Assistant assists the Information Management Officer. Her/his duties are similar to
the officiers and s/he is working under his/her direction.
Terms of Reference:
13.    Assistant Accountant
General:
The Accounts Assistant maintains the day to day accounts, payments and vouchers and
assists the Administrative Unit Chief in the running of the office of the Fund Board.
Specific:
1.     Financial:
- Maintains the accounts.
- Manage the petty cash account
- Ensure expenditures are made in accordance with Fund Board procedures
- Prepare periodic statements of accounts
- Reconcile the Fund-Board Bank Account
- Assist in audits of Fund Board
2.     Procurement:
- Following Fund-Board procurement guidelines in making local purchases
- Conducting purchasing of project goods and supplies
- Maintaining procurement and store inventory records
- Obtaining clearances for duty free project purchases
- Maintaining database to track payments
- Check receipt of office goods procured by Fund-Board
3.     Logistics:
- Arrange staff travel
- Maintain travel records
- manage travel advances and settlement of claims
- Help ensure that timely delivery of resources, financial and material as per contracts
- Make physical arrangements for project activities, including all logistical aspects of
workshops, field trips, etc.
- Provide other logistics as required by the project
- Assist in the management of the maintenance of office equipment and vehicles
4.     Personnel:
- maintain payroll and payroll records
- maintain personnel records, including sick/annual/admin. leave records
- maintain documentation of payments of consultants. Maintain personnel records including
time sheets and leave records
5.     Other:
-Assist in other administrative tasks as required

- other secretarial as required
- maintain SAJSO contract files, ensures all
contract decisions are documented and put to file
- manages calendar and travel of senior management
- provides technical support to other support staff
