NEPAL
RURAL WATER SUPPLY AND SANITATION PROJECT
Social Assessment
1.    Background.  Nepal remains one of the poorest countries in the world despite
efforts towards development in the last four decades. A burgeoning population (growth rate
of 2.5%) environmental degradation, a fragile resource base, poorly developed
infrastructure and an inefficient bureaucracy has further aggravated the situation. Current
social indicators show life expectancy at birth for men is 55 years and 53 for women,
making Nepal one of the three countries in the world where female life expectancy is less
than that of males. Infant mortality is 96 per 1000 live births and the prevalence of low
birth weight babies was 26% in 1991. The maternal mortality rate of 8.5 per 1000 is one of
the highest in the world.
2.    The literacy rate in Nepal is very low (35 percent) and is even lower for women (13
percent). The disparity in urban and rural female literacy rates are even more pronounced.
Enrolment in primary schools in 1991 was 61% for boys and 35% for girls. Economic
activity rate for men is 87.8% and that for women is only 43.5%. The female share of the
labor force is primarily concentrated in the agricultural sector.
3).    Ethnic diversity tend to follow the geophysical divisions of the country. There are
at least 25 ethnic groups each with its own distinct culture and heritage. The Tibeto-
Burman speaking peoples dominate the mountains in the north, the Nepali speaking are
concentrated in the middle hills and the Maithili and Bhopuri speaking are primarily found
in the terai. The majority of the population are Hindus (90%) followed by Buddhists (5%)
and Muslims (3%). A tradition of religious tolerance has resulted in a mixture of Buddhist
and Hindu elements in people's practices and beliefs. In the urban centers economic
necessity and modem education have minimized the utility of the caste based occupational
system. However, in the rural areas it continues to affect one's access to resources,
education and political power.
4.    Constraints. The major constraint that would be encountered in attempting to get
local people to work together to achieve project objectives is the dual problem of caste and
ethnic distinctions. The JAKPAS pilot project has demonstrated that in stratified
communities, the occupational caste groups (blacksmiths, tailors, shoemakers etc.) and/or
minority ethnic groups have not been able to participate effectively in the community action
planning (CAP) process because of attitudes which govern social interaction between
"high" and "low" castes. In addition, their lower literacy levels, lack of confidence to speak



- 160 -
Annex 16
Page 2 of 2
in public meetings and/or difficulty in communicating because of language barriers have
inhibited their full participation.
5.    The attitudes of men towards increasing women's participation would have an
impact on scheme sustainability. Most men believe that women cannot contribute to
discussions as they are illiterate or are too busy with childcare and/or household chores.
Culturally defined roles and responsibilities confine women to household maintenance
tasks, and deviations from cultural norms/values are usually frowned upon by village elders.
The pilot testing project demonstrated that this was more pronounced among the terai
groups, and in communities adhering to strict Hindu value systems.
6.    Assessment of Action Plan. Experience of the pilot project indicate that most
communities would lack technical skills and experience in cooperative actions such as
planning, constructing and maintaining common facilities. The proposed scheme cycle
which spans 36 months would allow SOs to assist communities to organize at a pace
appropriate to the local beneficiary group. The community action planning process (CAP)
would increase people's choices, increase their awareness of filth borne diseases and ensure
that technical design and scheme costs correspond to user needs.  The pilot project
demonstrated that interventions for community capacity building activities such as the
CAP process and nonformal education (NFE) have contributed towards bringing social
changes, such as a willingness to encourage women to take decision making roles, and
promoted the inclusion of occupational castes and/or other minority groups in the WUC to
improve services. To ensure disadvantaged groups fully participate in project benefits the
project has included complete community coverage, a registered water user group (W[G),
and a representative water user committee (WUC) with at least two women as criteria for
scheme selection. Trainings targeted to community members would contribute towards
institutionalizing the WUG for long term scheme sustainability. In addition, the women's
technical support services (WTSS) provides additional support to women to maximize
project benefits.
7.    The pilot project also demonstrated that when felt needs are properly identified a
high degree of beneficiary participation could be expected. This was demonstrated by
community willingness to contribute substantial time and cash to improve water supplies
thus contributing to scheme sustainability.  The project would assess the level of
need/demand and the degree of beneficiary participation prior to financing rural water
supply and sanitation schemes.
8.   The JAKPAS pilot project has substantially increased the capacity of SOs and
demonstrated the existence of many SOs that would be able to fulfil scheme
responsibilities, The project includes training for SOs to enable them to undertake their
tasks effectively. The project provides for monitoring visits in the development and
implementation phase to monitor SO compliance with contractual agreements, the quality
of outputs, and to assess the effectiveness of methods used in project implementation.



- 161 -
Annex 17
Page l of3
NEPAL
RURAL WATER SUPPLY AND SANITATION PROJECT
Terms of Reference for Technical Advisor
Position:          Technical Advisor
Duration:          Two years
Duty station:      Kathmandu, Nepal. Extensive in-country travel would be required
and some out of the country travel may be required.
Position Description:
1.    A Rural Water Supply and Sanitation Fund Development Board (the Board) has
been recently established by His Majesty's Government of Nepal to implement a demand
led, community based project, funded by IDA, whose objectives are to: (i) deliver
sustainable health and hygiene benefits to the rural population through improvements in
the water supply and sanitation facilities, (ii) improve rural real income by assisting women
identify ways to earn income from time saved in carrying water; and (iii) strengthen
governmental and non-governmental capabilities to undertake and sustain said efforts. The
focus of the project is to empower rural communities by using a demand driven approach
to service delivery and a participatory process to decision making to implement their water
supply and sanitation schemes with the assistance of support organizations (NGOs, CBOs,
private firms etc.) recruited by the Board.
2     The Board, therefore, needs to ensure that the demand driven approach and
community led participatory process to service delivery through support organizations
(SOs) is made effective. One of the many facets of this approach is to establish linkages
and good working relations with SOs. The challenge, therefore, is to operationalize within
the Board such demand driven approach and participatory process as well as the linkages
with SOs to make this service delivery mechanism effective. The prime responsibility of
the Technical Advisor (TA) is to help the Board meet this challenge.
Responsibilities:
3.    The Technical Advisor (TA) for the Rural Water Supply and Sanitation Fund
Development Board will have overall responsibility to:
(i)    Assist the ED in ensuring that the service delivery to the Communities follow a
demand led, community based approach, using an appropriate participatory
process thereby ensuring a high degree of scheme sustainability.



- 162 -
Annex 17
Page 2 of 3
(ii)   Assist the ED to ensure that the Board establishes linkages with the SOs, (NGOs,
CBOs etc.) such that a good line of communications is established between the
Board and the NGOs.
(iii)   Assist the ED to ensure that the community development aspects, fundamental to
this approach, are properly integrated into the Board implemention manual and
assist the Board in monitoring its implementation. Provide management assistance
to the Board to ensure that the Operational Manuals already prepared are
implemented, reviewed and refined as required taking into consideration the
lessons learnt during implementation. Assist in the development of Board
procedures, organization and coordination of project resources. The TA will
advise on institutional development aspects of the Board including program
development, monitoring, evaluation and technical appraisal.
(iv)   Review the operational Board management systems including personnel, financial,
technical appraisal, contract management and monitoring and evaluation (M&E)
systems and provide assistance and advice to the ED to make improvements, if
required. Assist the Executive Director (ED) in organizational management and
preparation and updating of operation manuals.
(v)   Advise as member of the technical appraisal committee (TAC) in the selection
process of Support Organization/schemes.
(vi).  Coordinate in consultation with the ED  all short term  technical assistance
(consultants) and staff development inputs to the Board.
(vii)  Provide technical inputs to the Human Resources Development (HRD)/Program
Development Unit, Technical Unit, Operations/Monitoring and Evaluation Unit,
and Administration Unit as and when needed.
(viii)  Review, comment and assist in the preparation of the workplans and progress
reports prepared by the Board. Based on such review, facilitate, assist and provide
on-the-job training to the Board staff to prepare/improve (i) annual workplans and
(ii) quarterly and annual progress reports on a timely manner and in formats that
address the need of the Board and donors.
Qualifications/Experience:
4     The minimum qualification/experience of the TA are as follows:
(i)    Masters Degree in Social Sciences from a recognized University.



- 163 -
Annex 17
Page 3 of 3
(ii)   At least ten years relevant experience including three years of international
experience in managing community development programs, foussing on demand
driven, community led approaches preferably in the water supply, sanitation, health
education and women oriented initiatives. The candidate should have hands on,
grassroots level field experiences in mobilizing communities and in working with
NGOs, CBOs, and private firms. Experience in Asia, particularly in South Asia,
will be preferable. The candidate should possess good knowledge of institutions
and have demonstrated operational experience.
(iii)   Excellent analytical and conceptual skills. Ability to communicate in English both
verbally and in writing in a concise and clear fashion. Ability to communicate
verbally in Nepali. Computer skills are essential.
